<UserId.>114266029332936876276<//UserId.>< Review>
This is one of my favorite places in downtown!  Whether I'm decompressing after a long day of work, or gearing up for a night out in San Jose I always find a good atmosphere. Kevin, the owner and main bartender is always welcoming and does a great job of making sure everyone is having a great time. Everytime I go in, it's easy to meet new friends in the comfortable vibe of this place.

The wine selection comes from a local vineyard and this place is the only vendor besides the vineyard itself. The selection is solid and each month there are two or three new wines in the rotation. If you're in the area you have to check it out!<//Review>

< review>
My grandparents took me here for the first time when I was about 3 or 4. Some of the best memories of my early childhood came from this airport and museum, so I had to just come back, literally a decade after my first visit here, to say thank you. < Review>
Ok I don‚Äôt know who this ‚Äújoe lunch-pale‚Äù guy is but I have been going to Chino airport for years. He is correct about the weeds. The airport management does a horrible job keeping up with them and half of the time you can‚Äôt see the signs or lights.

As for the Air Traffic Controllers they are some of the best around. A lot of pilots don‚Äôt know, but Chino airport is actually the 10th busiest airport in California and the controllers do an amazing job keeping everything moving safely. They do such a good job that the controllers at Chino airport were specifically mentioned in an article Cessna Magazine as outstanding controllers. There are times when they have new Controllers in training but every one of us has been that student at one point.
My guess is that Joe lunch-pale is one of those pilots that doesn‚Äôt pay attention, can‚Äôt listen to instructions or doesn‚Äôt fly often enough to be a competent pilot‚Ä¶or all of the above. There are several flight schools that are based at Chino airport so the controllers are used to dealing with student pilots. And in the event that one of those students messes up the controllers are usually very even tempered and inform the pilot what they did wrong so that they can fix it the next time around. There are times when there can be up to 12 or more aircraft in the patterns including several helicopters so delays can happen, but again 10th busiest airport in California. If you are IFR or Flight Following not only do they have to find a hole to get you out of the pattern but they have to coordinate with SoCal Departure to get a release and we all know how busy SoCal can get.
I have been up to visit the tower and was amazed at how professional the controllers are. They took the time to walk me around the tower explaining different equipment and positions that they work and they answered every question that I had. I never knew how much they had to do until actually seeing it from the tower. I just have to worry about my airplane but they have to worry about me and everyone else in and outside of their airspace and keep track of what everyone is doing and make sure they are doing what they are supposed to (students‚Ä¶and probably Joe). If you haven‚Äôt gotten the opportunity to tour the tower I highly recommend calling and scheduling a visit.

So if you haven‚Äôt been to Chino yet then please come on out. And if you are new to the area or the airport just tell the controllers it‚Äôs your first time or you are unfamiliar and they will go the extra mile to make sure you get where you need to go. As for Joe maybe if you tell them you are new to the area or a student pilot or unfamiliar with chino they can help explain what you did wrong. Listen up to instructions and follow them so the rest of us can get home safely. But then again maybe there is more to your story but my guess is that you got scolded by the controllers for doing something wrong and instead of finding out what it was you just wrote some vague review with no specifics</Review>

<Text>As much as I wanted to give Junk King a higher rating, my experience was far from seamless in what was already a stressful situation. Before booking for junk removal, I think everyone should at least know what to expect, so that they can avoid running through the same issues as I did.

After getting the news of my grandfather being transferred to hospice, and having to move my grandmother to live with us on short notice, we had to work as quickly as possible to clean out their house. Since it was my first time using a junk removal service, I called around to get a quote that would fit our budget. After meeting with several companies, it was down to Fred‚Äôs Junk Removal or Junk King.

Fred‚Äôs Junk Removal had a flat rate, but because I met the Junk King representatives in person and they seemed very nice and willing to work with our budget, I decided to book an appointment with them (plus, it doesn‚Äôt hurt when they have a guarantee to beat any written estimate). I tried calling the rep that had given me the quote, but it went to voicemail and indicated that I should call the San Diego call center for appointments.

After explaining the situation with my quote reference (2 pickup trucks, including some furniture removal) and telling the agent about Fred‚Äôs comparable 3 pickup truck flat rate of $297, I was put on hold so that the call center rep can make some calls for approval. When she got back to me with a price match of $295, I was relieved. I made sure to verify all the info and she confirmed that was the price for the job.

On the day of my appointment, I got Oscar (who I had met previously when I got my quote) and Fernando. According to Fernando, the confirmed quote I got from the call center didn‚Äôt match the one they had down, but rather the old estimate. After talking to his boss, he re-quoted me with $570, saying I already had a steal for that price and was free to go with Fred‚Äôs Junk Removal if I wanted to because they are busy and I was wasting their time. I felt like I was put in a bind to quickly make a decision, because not only did we had to clear the house by that day and catch a flight home right after, we now missed the opportunity to book with a cheaper option since it was so last minute. Had I known there were so much miscommunication within the company, where confirmation for details and prices of the job aren‚Äôt matching up and was even told that the call center ‚Äúdon‚Äôt know anything‚Äù, I would have went with a different company.

So before you book your appointment, make sure you aren‚Äôt on a time scrunch and confirm what the entire job entails, because you might have to pay more than you have to. The one star is for the speediness because they were able to knock it out in a short amount of time.< /Text>< Name>

<Text>As much as I wanted to give Junk King a higher rating, my experience was far from seamless in what was already a stressful situation. Before booking for junk removal, I think everyone should at least know what to expect, so that they can avoid running through the same issues as I did.

After getting the news of my grandfather being transferred to hospice, and having to move my grandmother to live with us on short notice, we had to work as quickly as possible to clean out their house. Since it was my first time using a junk removal service, I called around to get a quote that would fit our budget. After meeting with several companies, it was down to Fred‚Äôs Junk Removal or Junk King.

Fred‚Äôs Junk Removal had a flat rate, but because I met the Junk King representatives in person and they seemed very nice and willing to work with our budget, I decided to book an appointment with them (plus, it doesn‚Äôt hurt when they have a guarantee to beat any written estimate). I tried calling the rep that had given me the quote, but it went to voicemail and indicated that I should call the San Diego call center for appointments.

After explaining the situation with my quote reference (2 pickup trucks, including some furniture removal) and telling the agent about Fred‚Äôs comparable 3 pickup truck flat rate of $297, I was put on hold so that the call center rep can make some calls for approval. When she got back to me with a price match of $295, I was relieved. I made sure to verify all the info and she confirmed that was the price for the job.

On the day of my appointment, I got Oscar (who I had met previously when I got my quote) and Fernando. According to Fernando, the confirmed quote I got from the call center didn‚Äôt match the one they had down, but rather the old estimate. After talking to his boss, he re-quoted me with $570, saying I already had a steal for that price and was free to go with Fred‚Äôs Junk Removal if I wanted to because they are busy and I was wasting their time. I felt like I was put in a bind to quickly make a decision, because not only did we had to clear the house by that day and catch a flight home right after, we now missed the opportunity to book with a cheaper option since it was so last minute. Had I known there were so much miscommunication within the company, where confirmation for details and prices of the job aren‚Äôt matching up and was even told that the call center ‚Äúdon‚Äôt know anything‚Äù, I would have went with a different company.

So before you book your appointment, make sure you aren‚Äôt on a time scrunch and confirm what the entire job entails, because you might have to pay more than you have to. The one star is for the speediness because they were able to knock it out in a short amount of time.< /Text><Pictures>None<//Pictures>< response>

USE JUNK KING AND FORGET ABOUT CALLING ANYONE ELSE.  I don't live in SD and I was confronted with the enormous and emotionally painful task of cleaning out my dear parents home over Easter weekend. From the scheduling (so easy on the phone by a competent and knowledgeable rep) to communicating with the gentlemen in charge of the estate move out, everything was flawless.  I received an email confirmation and CJ and Austin called me about 30 min. before my appointment, showed up ON TIME, were extremely professional, in Junk King shirts, polite, pleasant and walked me through the process.  I have had professional movers move and pack me several times, and i have to say, CJ and Austin surpassed my prior experiences - and this one was tough, emotionally hard, as my parents had lived in this home for decades. These guys DO NOT REST.  They move. FAST.  LIKE SUPER FAST.  They work HARD. CJ and Austin were pleasant and so nice.  They didn't complain once and this was a very difficult task.  I cannot say enough about their open communication and professionalism.  They are truly service oriented AND know how to calmly deal with customers who are not only dealing with a difficult move out, but with grief and sadness as well.  They made all of it a little easier to cope with.   If you use Junk King, and I really hope you do, make sure you ask for CJ and Austin.  They will NOT disappoint you.  Great gentlemen who are hard workers.  Thank you CJ and Austin.</text>
